  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_613ebba6-dd6f-49e5-9217-d7cfc44fbcf9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer439164782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7139055179663271141">Oh my goodness. This is one of those that has a sappy romantic like myself sighing. A lonely, isolated man. A woman who 'has it together' or so it seems, but is a wreck on the inside. And they find each other.<br/><br/>The Beauty and the Beast retelling doesn't get old for me. After all, I am a die-hard romantic and a die-hard fairy tale lover. Pepper Pace does both so well here. Yet, instead of the Beast being grumpy and surly, Christopher is the sweetest teddy bear (although he probably resembles a Griz</span>
  <span id="freeText7139055179663271141" style="display:none">Oh my goodness. This is one of those that has a sappy romantic like myself sighing. A lonely, isolated man. A woman who 'has it together' or so it seems, but is a wreck on the inside. And they find each other.<br /><br />The Beauty and the Beast retelling doesn't get old for me. After all, I am a die-hard romantic and a die-hard fairy tale lover. Pepper Pace does both so well here. Yet, instead of the Beast being grumpy and surly, Christopher is the sweetest teddy bear (although he probably resembles a Grizzly bear) imaginable. I loved him! <br /><br />Pace challenges the reader here. Our Beauty has a significant weight problem. And the weight problem isn't her issue, but the emotions underneath it, the ones that caused her weight issues, and the results of them. If you've ever been overweight, you know how it is for Ashleigh. The comments that hit like barbs, because someone thinks they have the right to say something or the fact that they are insensitive, because they've never struggled with weight problems. The assumptions made about you because of your weight. <br /><br />On the other side, she doesn't make Ashleigh into a completely harmless victim. Ashleigh has some shallowness issues to work through. But that's the beauty of this story. She is able to see the beauty beneath the horrible scars and disfigurement that Christopher has. I truly loved the emotional connection between Christopher and Ashleigh. And there was also a very sensual component to this book, for romance readers who need that in their stories. Lots of spice and hot love scenes to go with an emotional love story that feels so authentic and timeless. <br /><br />When I got to 38% on my Kindle and love declarations were made, I wondered what else could happen in this book. Well, plenty. This is a love story about not just two people finding each other, but also also finding their way to healing. Making a life together in spite of obstacles they both face.<br /><br />When you read these kinds of stories, the stubborn person in you is determined to be upset if the problem is fixed, such as the heroine losing weight, or the hero getting his disfigurement repaired. But is that truly fair to the story for the characters not to go through that passage 'just because'? After all, it's easy to stay where you are. Even harder to take that step of faith to change something about yourself for the right reasons. In this case, the resolution made so much sense and only added to this story.<br /><br />If I could change anything? That's a matter of personal tastes, and I'm sure many will disagree with me. However, I could have done without some of the graphic language in the love scenes. While they were scintillating and the chemistry powerful, I guess I didn't need to read certain terms when it came to body parts. That's a small quibble.<br /><br />I'm personally no grammar stickler, but there were a couple issues there. I feel bad even pointing them out because a 100% accurate book doesn't necessarily tell a story that I love, like this somewhat imperfect one does. Overall, I found the writing very poised, professional, and so emotionally-stirring that I couldn't help but give this a five star rating.<br /><br />This was a beautiful love story. That's kind of ironic, because this story is about how what's on the surface doesn't show you everything. That what is at the heart is worth fighting for in the end.<br /><br />Highly recommended to romance readers who enjoy a more sensually descriptive love story, or just any old sap who can't resist a tried and true love story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7139055179663271141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_435601884" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435601884" />
    <a title="Shelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6080188-shelly"><img alt="Shelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389049874p2/6080188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/435601884?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly" href="/user/show/6080188-shelly">Shelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6080188-shelly?shelf=2012-fall-in-love-challenge">2012-fall-in-love-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6080188-shelly?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6080188-shelly?shelf=ir">ir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6080188-shelly?shelf=2012-ir-abc-cover-challenge">2012-ir-abc-cover-challenge</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer435601884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15208968268409439030">I appreciate a good retelling of an old tale. Beast tells the story of Ashleigh Dalton the plus-size person in her group of friends. She’s mid-thirties, successful in her career as an analyst for the government; looking from the outside in you would think she’s got it all together - except she’s just found out that her boyfriend of three years just married his ‘other’ girlfriend of six months. Lt. Christopher Jameson, 6’7” – 302lbs, Special Ops Marine, works in the same building as Ashleigh. Aft</span>
  <span id="freeText15208968268409439030" style="display:none">I appreciate a good retelling of an old tale. Beast tells the story of Ashleigh Dalton the plus-size person in her group of friends. She’s mid-thirties, successful in her career as an analyst for the government; looking from the outside in you would think she’s got it all together - except she’s just found out that her boyfriend of three years just married his ‘other’ girlfriend of six months. Lt. Christopher Jameson, 6’7” – 302lbs, Special Ops Marine, works in the same building as Ashleigh. After meeting in the company gym, the sparks fly between these two.<br /><br />I’ve read some of Pace’s other work and I think that there’s a lot of story telling talent there, so it was with a pleasant surprise that I saw this recent publication and I literally couldn’t wait to sit back and relax with Ashleigh and Christopher<br /><br />Ashleigh is one of the most immature characters I’ve read in a long time and I didn’t see a substantial change by the end. I should have suspected when she introduced herself to Christopher she not only gave him her name, she also gave him the spelled version ‘with a gh’. Really, you’re over 12 – that should have already fallen out of your introductory vocabulary. But I digress. After finding out about her very good looking boyfriend’s betrayal, Ashleigh decides that she’ll start losing weight because she’s realized that good looking men don’t want size 22 women (umm…gentlemen - is that true?). There’s a whole backstory about the Ashleigh’s behavior with her ex-boyfriend that I found very disturbing. After going to the gym a few mornings, the guy with the nice butt and great legs wearing a hoodie begins leaving his workout music for Ashleigh to enjoy setting the foundation for her and Christopher’s growing friendship. <br /><br />Christopher is a country boy through and through. He’s got the drawl and the homegrown manners that make his Mom proud. His friends, who are all Special Ops, call him Beast; not because of his misshaped facial aesthetics due to bilateral cleft palate but because he’s a beast on the field of combat. I really, really liked Christopher and I thought he could do so much better than Ashleigh. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One of Ashley’s many problems is not that she’s a foodie but that she’s bulimic and I’m not convinced that’s a topic handled well in this romance novel even more so complicated by pregnancy.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There are so many issues surrounding that and none of them were addressed with the gravity that they deserved.<br /><br />There were quite a few other things that I struggled with Ashleigh and Christopher’s behavior. The first time that they have sex, she tells him that she’s on the pill (remember she’s been ‘on the pill’ ONLY with a cheating ex-boyfriend) and Christopher says okay. You know what – you deserve what you get! I got past that. Because of her disease, Ashley’s a liar when it comes to her food binges especially after finding out that she’s been diagnosed with a life threatening illness. The list goes on and on of all the things I just couldn’t connect with and didn’t understand how a relatively mature businesswoman would feel and act the way Ashleigh did. <br /><br />Her best friends Kendra and Lance offered some interesting side commentary but in the end I didn’t care. Kendra could have been a good friend but she wasn’t given the chance. Her single dimension role was to be the pretty perfect friend who didn’t have anything else too offer. Lance got on my nerves with his excitable ‘screaming’, he was too over-the-top effeminate for my taste. Christopher’s family was the typical hillbilly folks who just couldn’t understand the government that Christopher served and Ashleigh worked for but they were smart enough to just want Christopher happy (insert a plethora of sarcasm). <br />I really wanted to enjoy this story but I just couldn’t, I found this story to be more twisted than fairytale.<br /><br />Happy Reading Folks!<br /><br />Rating: D<br /><br />Review also posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.RedHotBooks.com">http://www.RedHotBooks.com</a><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17473172822790822159"><b>5 out of 5 Stars! WOW WOW WOW!!!</b><br/><br/>I could not put this book down. I love absolutely everything about this story. This one is a gem that will certainly touch your heart. To my core I felt what these two main characters were feeling.<br/><br/>Christopher! Totally fell in love with this man. Don't think I've ever read such a perfect combination of an Alpha/Beta male on the written page. Couldn't imagine what his shoes would feel like if I were the one who had to wear them, but I felt him just the same.<br/><br/>Ashleigh</span>
  <span id="freeText17473172822790822159" style="display:none"><b>5 out of 5 Stars! WOW WOW WOW!!!</b><br /><br />I could not put this book down. I love absolutely everything about this story. This one is a gem that will certainly touch your heart. To my core I felt what these two main characters were feeling.<br /><br />Christopher! Totally fell in love with this man. Don't think I've ever read such a perfect combination of an Alpha/Beta male on the written page. Couldn't imagine what his shoes would feel like if I were the one who had to wear them, but I felt him just the same.<br /><br />Ashleigh- I love her. I cried with and for her. Cheered her on. Got ticked &amp; screamed at her, but ultimately just prayed her personal prison of suffering would end. Cos the bottom line is, she deserved better. Way better. These two (Christopher &amp; Ashleigh) were beautiful together. Just beautiful. Who they are in their own rite, and who they became not just for themselves, but for each other was nothing short of incredible.<br /><br />I've seen in some reviews where others felt that the pace of this one slows in some areas of the story. IMO, the pacing was perfect. It kept me interested and eager to know what was going to happen next. I think this one flows beautifully.<br /><br />You have alot of interesting secondary characters &amp; plots that blend great within the story. This story, I would call an "Onion" of the fiction world. There are definitely alot of layers peeled back as you go. Each one that is revealed is just as intriguing, beautiful, heartfelt, and shocking in it's own rite. <br /><br />This one is a gripping, romantic, erotic, emotional, &amp; all consuming read. I HIGHLY recommend that you read it :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11528408559521317712">I loved this.<br/><br/>I finished reading it and I was just "awwwwww"<br/><br/>Tbh, I love this sort of story. <br/><br/>A few issues I had would be that you would be reading and all of a sudden it was a week, 2 weeks, a month later. occasionally, the timeline would be confused, at one point, it was one day since the hero had spoken to someone, and then in the next paragraph in the same scene it was a month since he had spoken to that someone.<br/><br/>But, only very minor issues, and it was still 5 stars for me, as I just loved the s</span>
  <span id="freeText11528408559521317712" style="display:none">I loved this.<br /><br />I finished reading it and I was just "awwwwww"<br /><br />Tbh, I love this sort of story. <br /><br />A few issues I had would be that you would be reading and all of a sudden it was a week, 2 weeks, a month later. occasionally, the timeline would be confused, at one point, it was one day since the hero had spoken to someone, and then in the next paragraph in the same scene it was a month since he had spoken to that someone.<br /><br />But, only very minor issues, and it was still 5 stars for me, as I just loved the story and the characters.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2449659840979227401"><i>Written August 29, 2014</i><br/><br/><b>3 1/2 Stars - Nice, thoughtful and romantic ... and two lovable characters</b><br/><br/>A twisted <i>Beauty & Beast romance</i>. — A Beast with a destroyed face and a plus sized Beauty who has identity issues. <br/><br/><a href='http://yoursmiles.org/t-sport.php?page=5' rel='nofollow noopener'>

She is a</span>
  <span id="freeText2449659840979227401" style="display:none"><i>Written August 29, 2014</i><br><br><b>3 1/2 Stars - Nice, thoughtful and romantic ... and two lovable characters</b><br><br>A twisted <i>Beauty &amp; Beast romance</i>. — A Beast with a destroyed face and a plus sized Beauty who has identity issues. <br><br><a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-sport.php?page=5" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392673220ra/8592608.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-sport.php?page=5" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392673220ra/8592608.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-sport.php?page=5" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392673220ra/8592608.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>A <s>good</s> <u>nice</u> one! I liked to listening to this story, well narrated and a kind of simple ears entertainment.<br><br>********************************************************<br><br><b>Ashleigh Dalton is a short plump (plus-size)</b>, beautiful light-skinned Af-Am woman in her mid-thirties. She is a smart, friendly, funny and successful in her career, as an analyst for the government, but she is still a single waiting for <i>Mr Tall Gorgeous Dream Man</i>. Ashleigh thought she maybe already had that man but she’s just found out that her so called boyfriend of three years just married his "other" girlfriend (of six months). A slim and slender girl of course!!! <br><br>~ Life kind of sucks for dear Ashleigh, and everything is mostly because she is too chunky and fat (her opinion). Nice goodlooking men don't want to date the chubby girls - at least not as future girlfriends or wifes. ~ Time to make a difference: be at the gym every morning at 6:30. ...Puffing and panting, it's hard work.<br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/albums/w615/Li64/Diverse/?action=view&amp;current=17ab6a6248a804991dba8d3524e5e934_zps4e0a819c.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409344482i/10968411.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><b>Special Ops Marine, Lt. Christopher Jameson</b>, is a shy huge (6.7) white <i>country boy</i>, who works with security in the same building as Ashleigh. He was born with misshaped facial aesthetics due to <i>bilateral cleft palate</i>. Sadly was his parents poor people and with that were these defects unfortunately not cared for by the best surgeons and doctors then when he was a small child. The scars are to be honest horrifying but his aka-name, <i>Beast</i>, has Christopher primarily for his very tough strong style on the battlefield. <br><br>~ Christopher runs on the treadmill, is muscular and well shaped, eat lots of healthy food, plays guitar and has a cat - but otherwise he's very lonely. Most often, he pulls the hood over his head and run past so that no one will stare at him.<br><br> <b>... Like, you guessed, they meet in the basement gym</b> and soonish the sparks fly between these two.<br><br>********************************************************<br><br><b>Overall is <i>Beast</i> an sweet important story</b>. It deals with many important topics and current issues in a good and natural way. It is about your appearance, dieting, food and nutrition, fitness and exercise, family and skin-color, and various prejudices. <br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/albums/w615/Li64/Diverse/?action=view&amp;current=17ab6a6248a804991dba8d3524e5e934_zps4e0a819c.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409344482i/10968411.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><b>The Beast is kind and safe - The Beauty must find her way</b> ~ Christopher &amp; Ashleigh are two nice main charaters. I liked them and I enyoyed their story. I felt for them and with them. They were a perfect match. They are both two young lonly characters seeking for love. They have both many flaws and external shortcomings, an ugly scared face and a too plump body, compared to today's appearance ideals. This is of course a romance, and you know what happens in romances. <br><br><i>1) Lose weight and work off a few pounds of fat and let your beautiful hair gently blowing free from tight knots. 2) Put away any ugly glasses and buy a very sexy dress. 3) Put on your sexiest heels and new minimal black lace underwear - <br><b>...and it's all easy fixed</b>. </i><br><br>A lucky romance Cinderella, or a male Cinder, has blossomed again. ~ Exactly that way wasn't it this time, but almost. ~ I must point out that they were both very, very much worth it. <br><br>********************************************************<br><br><b>This narrator <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8505578.LaShone_Garth" title="LaShone Garth" rel="nofollow noopener">LaShone Garth</a> made it good in many ways</b>. I don't know, but I felt that she lisps a little bit - very charmingly. She also had a soft girlie voice (black?) for Ashleigh. I liked her voice. <br><br>~ Listening to smexy hot scenes? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sometimes it feels both embarrassing and a bit corny to listening to some sexy moanings and hot mutterings read high and loud for you by a narrator. (I usually turn down the volume and think about when it's time to change the laundry in the washing machine, or what is needed for dinner, or the upcoming review.)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>********************************************************<br><br><b>The first half of the book was very promising and really good</b>. I had big hopes for something new and fresh, but then it started to sway slowly. Unfortunately a little too much in the end. The heroine Ashleigh became more and more an anxious damsel in distress instead of a tough independent girl. Perhaps ended it also a bit too sugary sweet. I kind of missed my two very interesting characters who were there first. Left was almost a new pair of <i>Barbie &amp; Ken</i>. ~ Not my <i>Beauty &amp; Beast</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/albums/w615/Li64/Cartoon/cute%20love%20drawings/?action=view&amp;current=34b12a9442c88e0bfb1f6c53e68c1bfd_zps7492b51c.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409161386i/10941718.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br>But regardless everything: <i>Beast</i> actually was a quite nice goodfeel romance. <br><br><b>I LIKE - Yes I do, it is a B&amp;B story</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_537656983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537656983" />
    <a title="Vallsykes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5164414-vallsykes"><img alt="Vallsykes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367067514p2/5164414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537656983?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vallsykes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vallsykes" href="/user/show/5164414-vallsykes">Vallsykes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like twists on a fairy tale</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=beautifully-beta">beautifully-beta</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=setting-is-a-great-character">setting-is-a-great-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=sugar-coma">sugar-coma</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=interracial-gems">interracial-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=great-storyline">great-storyline</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=surprisingly-good">surprisingly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5164414-vallsykes?shelf=weight-issues">weight-issues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537656983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17156550543430771216"><b>
  <blockquote>“I’m learning, sweetheart. Just…please be patient with me. It’s hard to undo a lifetime of insecurities.” <br/><br/>She gave him a solemn look. “I know.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><b>3.5 stars</b> for overall plot<br/><b>4 stars</b> for <i> the story it wants to be</i><br/><br/>This story is a spin on the old tale, <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, but really, the beast is more than a scarred man who falls in love with a beauty.<br/><br/>In this story, both the hero and the heroine carry a beast inside of them, the hero with his inward loneliness and outward isolation due to his defor</span>
  <span id="freeText17156550543430771216" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“I’m learning, sweetheart. Just…please be patient with me. It’s hard to undo a lifetime of insecurities.” <br /><br />She gave him a solemn look. “I know.”</blockquote>
</b><br /><b>3.5 stars</b> for overall plot<br /><b>4 stars</b> for <i> the story it wants to be</i><br /><br />This story is a spin on the old tale, <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, but really, the beast is more than a scarred man who falls in love with a beauty.<br /><br />In this story, both the hero and the heroine carry a beast inside of them, the hero with his inward loneliness and outward isolation due to his deformity, the heroine with her self-seeking vanity and battle with obesity. Furthermore, there are outside "beasts" that are battled as well, in the form of other people's superficiality, prejudices and ignorance. Yet these are never so <i>strong</i> as the struggle both the hero and heroine face as they learn to trust and accept that "good" IS out there, just waiting for them to grasp it. To "see" it! Benefit from the <i>beauty of it</i>.<br /><br /><i>Beast</i> is aptly named even if the cover is a poor complement. It hits upon some deep issues, sometimes, in <i>almost</i> very poignant ways(meaning:<i>I was touched, but not floored by them</i>). More to the point, some changes in the characters' circumstances, I questioned, but totally understood why this writer took those routes.<br /><br />This is one of those times when I, as a reader, was taken by the sentiment and intentions in the author's purpose, but recognized some <i>slight</i> mis-fires in execution. It's a story that's written a little rough-around-the-edges, but it MERITS attention. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17156550543430771216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13864735594718361610">I really wanted to like this story, but there were a few things that prevented that. The first and foremost was the lack of copy editing. I realize that most people don't care about grammar, but there were so many mistakes, I was taken right out of the story. The constant switching of POV made my head spin. Lastly, I wanted a bit more tension between the main characters before they got together.</span>

<div id="review_547951269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547951269" />
    <a title="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583236251p2/3575839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/547951269?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" href="/user/show/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog">Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kristen Ashley fans!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=fugly-cover">fugly-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=best-of-the-best-2013">best-of-the-best-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=faves-couple-made-in-heaven">faves-couple-made-in-heaven</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-contemporary-romance">genre-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-mad-bad-and-dangerous-to-know">hero-mad-bad-and-dangerous-to-know</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=faves-kings-of-the-harem">faves-kings-of-the-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-hot-male-in-my-harem">hero-hot-male-in-my-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-virgin-or-inexperienced">hero-virgin-or-inexperienced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-i-wanna-hug">hero-i-wanna-hug</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer547951269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1910726542952395850">Christopher aka "Beast" has a badly mangled face, all people ever see when they look at his scarred face and massive body is a monster, never really knowing the man he is underneath. Ashleigh has had her heartbroken once again, men thinking they can walk all over her just because she is plus sized. When the two meet can they both get past their own prejudices and insecurities and create their own Beauty & the Beast fairytale?<br/><br/>I may have found a new author to stalk, Pepper Pace has completely blow</span>
  <span id="freeText1910726542952395850" style="display:none">Christopher aka "Beast" has a badly mangled face, all people ever see when they look at his scarred face and massive body is a monster, never really knowing the man he is underneath. Ashleigh has had her heartbroken once again, men thinking they can walk all over her just because she is plus sized. When the two meet can they both get past their own prejudices and insecurities and create their own Beauty &amp; the Beast fairytale?<br /><br />I may have found a new author to stalk, Pepper Pace has completely blown me away with this book! I love a good Beauty and the Beast retelling, so chucking in a six and half foot tall marine and a plus sized heroine and I am in book heaven with no intention of leaving. <br /><br />As soon as I started reading about Beast, I knew I would love him he was a gentle giant and extremely lonely as no one, especially women, saw past his disfigured face. When I say disfigured I mean Phantom of the Opera style scarred and not just a little scar that goes across his check and make him look both sexy and dangerous. I liked that Ms Pace was brave enough to go all out and make a genuinely scary and ugly looking hero and although I like to say and think I would never judge someone by looking at their face, I am honest enough to say that I very well might have done, and if I had I would have lost out on one amazing guy, he is definitely having a starring role in my book boyfriend harem. <br /><br />With Ashleigh, it took me a while to warm up to her and it seemed liked it was deliberate, she was a bit shallow and despite knowing people judged her by her appearance she did exactly the same to everyone else. But as the book progressed and you got to know Ashleigh and you see her and Christopher's relationship bloom I found myself starting to really like and respect her. <br /><br />This was a fabulous romance, it was sweet but intense; the chemistry between Chris and Ashleigh built gradually and then exploded off the page. <i>Beast</i> was solely focused on the two main characters it had no minor intrigue or suspense plot going on in the background; there were no crazy exes or long forgotten enemies, I liked that it unashamedly followed the romance without adding unnecessary plot elements in. <br /><br />This was a fantastic read, already I can feel the urge to reread it, it had unforgettable main characters, a passionate romance and although the writing may not be very polished it made up for it with lots of heart. I highly recommend this!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1910726542952395850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1014779188160198185">Description: When plus-size beauty, Ashleigh, meets Chris, a “beast” of a marine with a face disfigured from a cleft palate at the gym, sparks fly. But can she overcome her baggage and make an HEA happen with the best man she’s ever had the honor of dating? BEAST quite deservedly made it to the semi-final rounds of this year’s Amazon Breakthrough Novel Award contest.<br/><br/>The Good: I’m so late on this, that I doubt anyone who reads this review hasn’t actually already read the book yet. But I’m going t</span>
  <span id="freeText1014779188160198185" style="display:none">Description: When plus-size beauty, Ashleigh, meets Chris, a “beast” of a marine with a face disfigured from a cleft palate at the gym, sparks fly. But can she overcome her baggage and make an HEA happen with the best man she’s ever had the honor of dating? BEAST quite deservedly made it to the semi-final rounds of this year’s Amazon Breakthrough Novel Award contest.<br /><br />The Good: I’m so late on this, that I doubt anyone who reads this review hasn’t actually already read the book yet. But I’m going to just go ahead and add to the gush fest.<br /><br />This book is sooooooo good. I love that the heroine is plus-sized and struggles with both self-esteem issues and Type 2 diabetes. Ashleigh is incredibly relatable and I could not recommend this book more to women with similar issues.<br /><br />You will be hard put not to fall in love with Christopher, he’s such a wonderful and caring hero, a sensitive guy with an alpha body, you can’t beat that. Loved his loneliness, loved his damaged face, loved everything about this guy–he’s so well-drawn. <br /><br />And as for his and Ashleigh’s relationship, I’ll quote the note I made on my Kindle while reading this: “so fucking romantic.”<br />BEAST is a very full and satisfying book and totally worth the price–in fact, I would say it’s underpriced. Oh, and the sex scenes are great.<br /><br />The Bad: The too long last act and epilogue throws off the book’s overall structure. You totally won’t mind, though, as these characters are hard to say goodbye to. Also, see editing issues.<br /><br />The Naughty: Erotic. Sex in the woods. Lots and lots of sex.<br /><br />Editing issues: My version was purchased before the ABNA version came out, so the following may no longer be of issue. Several typos. Weirdly formatted on my Kindle with random paragraph breaks. Loads of missing commas.<br /><br />Publisher: Pepper Pace<br /><br />Length: 367 pages<br /><br />Final Grade: A<br /><br />Happy Reading,<br />Theodora from irbookreviews.com</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14430992703529095985"> We need to talk about this book. I have so many conflicting feelings you guys. <br/>1. The introduction is so minimal and then we immediately jump into the protagonist wanting to do real physical damage to her beau (DeAngelo). Now I understand why. You needed a hook to bring your readers in. I do get that. However, the moment I start reading your editing is the most distracting thing. Perhaps because the ENTIRE (and I do not exaggerate, I do mean the entire) work is so obviously unedited. There are </span>
  <span id="freeText14430992703529095985" style="display:none"> We need to talk about this book. I have so many conflicting feelings you guys. <br />1. The introduction is so minimal and then we immediately jump into the protagonist wanting to do real physical damage to her beau (DeAngelo). Now I understand why. You needed a hook to bring your readers in. I do get that. However, the moment I start reading your editing is the most distracting thing. Perhaps because the ENTIRE (and I do not exaggerate, I do mean the entire) work is so obviously unedited. There are websites for that (grammarly for example). <br />2. Your over use of ellipses takes away from every single dramatic moment you mean for them to help. An ellipsis is used to either signify the omission of words, or the trailing off of a sentence, not the changing of a thought or a dramatic pause. <br />3. Your entire first scene is totally copied from a Jill Scott : <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=R0UDyhlYYPc" rel="nofollow noopener">song</a>, and I need you to know that I am on to you. <br />4. I love Lance, but he is problematic, and we will come back to that later on. As the single solitary fat female friend in my social circle, I rather Identify with being set up with someone I'm not remotely interested in. However, the problem I have is that Kendra wasn't worried about Ash being attracted to who she picked for her, she just wanted Ash to settle. First strike against Kendra. Oh my goodness, you don't even know how happy it made me to find out that Christopher also eats his leftover Spaghetti cold. <br />5. My dear friend, you cannot at all do metaphors. It's okay. They aren't for everyone. That description for his ass being like two boulders is first and foremost terrible, and secondly, it is in no way artful of properly descriptive. Boulder booty? Really Pepper? Really? <br />6. There is no way in Hell that this woman saw this man's back muscles and though " Nice". You're bullshitting. I'm on to you. <br />7. Okay. The rage I felt when those stupid mother fuckers made fun of her while she was working out was so unholy. I know that. I live that everyday. It's so real. THAT is relatable.<br />8. I mean I knew they called him beast, I assumed it was because of his size, not because of his disfigurement. Kudos on the curveball. That is good writing.<br />9. Pepper now I need you to sit down and realize that there is NO WAY i'm going to believe this heffa fainted all of three times. I'm not doing it. it is not only unrealistic but it's also bullshit. Step ya cookies up pep.<br />10. You are not about to tell me that " Warm buttered toast" Is the metaphor you are using to describe this woman Pepper Pace. I know you are a black woman. You can do better. Even if you have to use "brown sugar" It's better that goddamned " Warm buttered toast". You have GOT to do better, because that metaphor is SORELY lacking.<br />11. This is where I realized Christopher had tree trunk thighs. Well done. Mazel Tov. Nicely done.<br />12. Oh my! The southern gentleman you created him to be is flawlessly structured. Very very nice Pep.<br />13. Why would you say that she looked like buttered toast, and then make them give her a piece of buttered toast Pepper? What the hell is wrong with you?<br />14. Girl if you don't start editing your goddamned books. THERE IS NEVER A COMMA BETWEEN TOUGH OR COOKIE WHEN YOU ARE SAYING SOMEONE IS A TOUGH COOKIE. YOU ONLY NEED A COMMA TO SIGNIFY A GODDAMNED PAUSE. JESUS PEPPER, GET IT TOGETHER.<br />15. Why the fuck did DeAngelo's BUM ASS just pop up at the hospital, and why did her friends just let him stay? I don't give a single solitary fuck if he was an emergency contact. They are the WORST friends for not telling him to get the hell out of that hospital room. " I'm your friend too" NO THE FUCK YOU ARE NOT. <br />16. Pepper that dismissal is everything I ever needed. She better tell DeAngelo " Goodluck. Goodbye. And lose my number." Tiny lil problem here though Pep. YOU CANNOT START A SENTENCE WITH THE WORD AND UNLESS THERE IS A PROPERLY PLACED COMMA. STEP YOUR GRAMMAR UP. EDIT YOUR WRITING.<br />17. Christopher is such a cutie patootie. I love that he's nervous about asking her out, but there is NO WAY he is that oblivious. She doesn't hide her emotion OR her attraction well.<br />20. I don't give a fuck if Debbie's old married with kids ass come to apologize to Christopher. FUCK. DEBBIE. Fifteen year old me would have dated the shit out of fifteen year old Chris. Debbie can eat a dick.<br />21. THANK GOD! I swear to god I thought he would never ask her out.<br />22. There is nothing on this Earth that is more attractive to me than a man who knows how to cook. Praise the Lord! <br />23. DAAAAAAAMN PEPPER. BACK AT IT AGAIN WITH THAT TERRIBLE TOAST METAPHOR.<br />24. You can do better. " Sex" is a played out word to use for " VAGINA". Quit your shit Pepper.<br />25. " Delicious fountain". Pepper bihh P L E A S E STOP.<br />26. "She’d never been this close to a white man’s penis" Didn't even need to be said. Unnecessary. See what happens when you don't fucking edit Pepper? You leave stupid shit in your writing.<br />27. " Hard pipe" YOU. NEED. TO. DO. BETTER. <br />28. I have never been so worried about anyone walking into a house full of country white people in my LIFE. <br />29. They fuckin again? Damn fam.<br />30. " Slick opening" is tactless and tasteless and you KNOW it. DO BETTER PEPPER. BE BETTER PEPPER.<br />31. Yo HOW MANY TIMES ARE THEY ABOUT TO FUCK DUDE?!?! This is all like with in a two page span. SLOW THE FUCK DOWN PEPPER.<br />32. This is one reason Lance is problematic. THERE IS NO SUCH THING AS BEING A BLACK WOMAN IN HEART. THAT IS NOT A JOKE. THAT IS NOT FUNNY. <br />33. You are KILLING me. How could he go missing like that?!?! LITERALLY WHAT THE FUCK PEPPER.<br />34. Her being pregnant is predictable. Her being athletically thin is an ABSOLUTE cop out. You know that. It's the lazy way out. You also lose your message that way Pep.<br />35. "EMPTIES THE CONTENTS OF HIS TESTICLES INTO HER WOMB" you need someone standing over your shoulder just telling you not to write tasteless tactless shit because WOW, was that unnecessary. It also almost made me put the book down Pep. You need to be more careful.<br />36. Please abandon metaphors Pepper Pace. They are not for you.<br />37. I don't even know how many more times I am gong to say this Pepper, but BITCH EDIT YOUR SHIT. <br />38. Pepper. What is the purpose of DeAngelo showing up yet AGAIN. He is scum. We know this. Unnecessary drama takes away from a good story even MORE than shitty grammar and poor editing.<br />39. PEPPER YOU DON'T KNOW HOW TO EDIT. YOU ALSO DO NOT HAVE ANY CONCEPT OF PROPER GRAMMAR. AND YET, YOU SOMEHOW FIGURED OUT THAT THE WORD CALLIPYGIAN BELONGS IN YOUR WORK. WELL I HAVE SOME NEWS FOR YOU. IT DOESN'T FIT TOO WELL IN THE SAME SENTENCE AS TWO ERRONEOUSLY USED ELLIPSES, I'LL TELL YOU THAT MUCH.<br />40. Good Lord! Ash's sisters are absolute vipers. How sad. That makes me hurt for her.<br /><br />In closing, I will say that Ash losing the weight for herself and becoming healthier for her is good but there is ABSOLUTELY no need for her to be stick thin. You lose your message that way. You also are very unrealistic in writing that Chris was some Adonis after those surgeries. What little bit of your message you could have salvaged was ruined in him becoming miraculously handsome. Your editing was the MAJOR overall issue. You either need a new editor, or you need to hire someone to look your shit over, because it distracted me through the ENTIRE book. **mic drop**<br /> </span>

<div id="review_858864185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858864185" />
    <a title="McGee Magoo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17755136-mcgee-magoo"><img alt="McGee Magoo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551480048p2/17755136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858864185?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="McGee Magoo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="McGee Magoo" href="/user/show/17755136-mcgee-magoo">McGee Magoo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781480022119" href="/book/show/19655215-beast">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17755136-mcgee-magoo?shelf=bbw-loses-weight">bbw-loses-weight</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17755136-mcgee-magoo?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17755136-mcgee-magoo?shelf=disabled-disfigured-h-h">disabled-disfigured-h-h</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17755136-mcgee-magoo?shelf=cop-firefighter-military-hero">cop-firefighter-military-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17755136-mcgee-magoo?shelf=inter-racial">inter-racial</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858864185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17530785377511366460">I feel like I can't even come up with a review good enough for this book. Or one that doesn't have spoilers. <br/><br/>There are just some tropes that get to me, you know? If an M/C is disfigured or disabled--BRING IT ON! I want to read that book ASAP. The angst level is so deliciously high, I'm in love by the time I've finished reading the synopsis. Okay, add to that a heroine that is a BBW (Big Beautiful Woman)--which is another of my favorite things--and I'm practically weeping tears of joy. But wait--</span>
  <span id="freeText17530785377511366460" style="display:none">I feel like I can't even come up with a review good enough for this book. Or one that doesn't have spoilers. <br /><br />There are just some tropes that get to me, you know? If an M/C is disfigured or disabled--BRING IT ON! I want to read that book ASAP. The angst level is so deliciously high, I'm in love by the time I've finished reading the synopsis. Okay, add to that a heroine that is a BBW (Big Beautiful Woman)--which is another of my favorite things--and I'm practically weeping tears of joy. But wait--can it be?--another potential angst-creating plot-twist?? An inter-racial romance?! **SWOONING--SLAPPING FACE TO REGAIN CONSCIOUSNESS** Do you hear the angels singing? Because I do. <br /><br />And on a side-note, in the introduction, the author Pepper Pace says this: "...there are some tears as well as some laughs but there is also plenty of very hot sex." PLUS--I got this at a bargain for 99 pennies on Amazon. The <i>synopsis</i> was worth 99 cents, okay. It could fuel fantasies for years.<br /><br />You're probably thinking that there I was, not even done reading the Introduction and I'd already deemed this a 5-star read, which, unfortunately might have set me up for a huge let-down. And I'll admit that the angst level didn't quite meet my expectation. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ But part of me was relieved that I didn't have to endure watching Christopher be harassed or made fun of or anything that was cruel. And while Ashleigh's weight and image and health issues were a key point in the story, it didn't cause any too great amount of distress for me, either. AND considering that Christopher was white and his family (who he was very close to) were damn near hill-billies, I figured we'd get some conflict about race from that angle. In a way I was happy that the story really didn't go there, but it was the last chance for some real meaty "Oh, my God", conflict. So, hardly anyone cared that Christopher didn't have a face, hardly anyone cared that she was fat and no one cared that they were an inter-racial couple.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Yet, I still absolutely loved it. Pepper Pace knows how to tell a story and she sure knows how to create multi-faceted characters. Were there a few grammar/spelling mistakes? Yes--but the only thing that comes to mind was the word "in" used where "and" should have been. That's it--so not worth docking any stars. Was it a little cliched? Yeah, but this is romance--romance that says right away that this is a modern-day fairy tale. If "cliche" bothers you, you're reading the wrong genre. And while I'm mentioning the "fairy-tale" aspect to this, remember that this is a take on Beauty and the Beast and magic did abound in that tale, so expect some less-than-believable stuff to happen.<br /><br />I devoured this book and can't wait to try out other Pepper Pace books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17530785377511366460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_858926683" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858926683" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7513972-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466967967p2/7513972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858926683?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/7513972-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781480022119" href="/book/show/19655215-beast">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7513972-victoria?shelf=4-5-star-reads">4-5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7513972-victoria?shelf=best-book-boyfriends">best-book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7513972-victoria?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7513972-victoria?shelf=wounded-warrior">wounded-warrior</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858926683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3951122388606122798"><b>What do you get when an overweight, slightly shallow black woman meets a disfigured, lonely, white Marine? A great twist on an old classic!</b><br/><br/>Beast by Pepper Pace was a totally random pick for me and a little different than the normal romances I pick out. I saw someone post that it was on sale, read the blurb, and immediately downloaded it. The story was a great mix of a lot of things I really like. It was part sweet and part sexy, part real, part fairy tale. There was definitely some humor thrown </span>
  <span id="freeText3951122388606122798" style="display:none"><b>What do you get when an overweight, slightly shallow black woman meets a disfigured, lonely, white Marine? A great twist on an old classic!</b><br /><br />Beast by Pepper Pace was a totally random pick for me and a little different than the normal romances I pick out. I saw someone post that it was on sale, read the blurb, and immediately downloaded it. The story was a great mix of a lot of things I really like. It was part sweet and part sexy, part real, part fairy tale. There was definitely some humor thrown in too! <br /><br />The story was well written and was easy to read. The characters were well developed and I loved both. Ashleigh was a likable heroine but had some obvious flaws. Outside of being a bit shallow, she had some pretty serious self-esteem issues which resulted in different types of destructive behavior, both emotional and physical. I get sick of perfect heroines and maybe that's why I really liked Ashleigh so much. She was smart, successful, and very likable, flaws and all! <br /><br />I’m not African American and I’ve never been obese but that didn’t stop me from identifying with certain aspects of Ashleigh’s personality. A few things really resonated with me , some made me laugh and others made me cringe.<br /><br /><b>She always wished that she was the star of a John Hughes movie because then she would always have a happy ending. There would be some achingly handsome guy holding a boom box above his head right outside her window, or the school jock would dump the cheerleader girlfriend for her. But in reality the cheerleader always got the man.</b><br /><br />The fact that Lance was obsessed with those movies as much as Ashleigh was had me laughing more than once. Maybe it's my age, but who doesn’t love the Breakfast Club and Pretty in Pink? The fact that they had a running commentary on Andy not choosing Ducky was classic!<br /><br />When Ashleigh begins working out and is totally psyching herself out to work harder… I’ve totally done that.<br /><br /><b>Then she began pedaling. I’m getting skinnier, she thought. Each pedal I’m getting skinnier. Each bead of sweat is a drop of fat melting off my body. Push it girl, push it…</b><br /><br />And the part that made me cringe? The negative thoughts Ashleigh has about herself. I’ve definitely had periods in my life where I can look back and realize I put alot of pressure on myself to be a certain way (someone better, someone thinner, someone smarter). I think as woman, there are definitely a lot of pressures that can build up and result in really negative internal thoughts. Reading the negativity that was such a part of Ashleigh’s mindset just made me remember how easy it is to create certain standards for ourselves that can be really difficult to achieve.<br /><br /><b>I am not good enough. I am a selfish, shallow, slut, bitch.<br />… I wish I was anybody but me. </b><br /><br />I loved the development that I saw in Ashleigh and the self-acceptance of both herself and others. I think the author did a great job of showing the journey Asheigh goes on to get to a healthier place, especially for a lighter book like Beast.<br /><br /><b>The world makes you feel ugly. Your friends when they say, ‘if only you would lose weight,’ are really saying, ‘you are not as good as the rest of us.’” Kendra gave her a hurt look. “Oh, they don’t mean to hurt you or pass judgment or call you ugly. But in my case, I put two and two together and what I came up with is that I wasn’t good enough. But, as long as I could have beautiful men loving me I could pretend. <br /><br />“I wish I knew then what I know now; it doesn’t matter what people look like on the outside, because if you love them they are beautiful.”</b><br /><br />As much as I identified with Ashleigh, Christoper stole the show for me. He is the type of character that you can't help but love. I absolutely adored Christopher from the moment he was introduced until the very last page. He is the type of hero you can’t help rooting for. I don’t want to give anything away but will say that I was a little disappointed when it was revealed where Chris had been on his “mission”. (After thinking about it though, I’m glad he got the mission he did.)<br /><br />The romance was sweet and sexy, a favorite mix of mine!<br /><br /><b>“Your lips are so perfect.” He said softly. And then she felt his soft mouth kissing her lightly. “You are so damn beautiful…” <br /><br />She opened her eyes and gave him a serious look. “Christopher… you are the one that’s beautiful.” She lifted her head. “And not just on the inside. You’re beautiful on the outside, too. To me… you’re perfect.” <br /><br />She could see several emotions move across his face before his eyes half closed and his light eyelashes created a frame through which she could see the eyes that she loved so much. And they watched her with a little bit of trepidation. <br /><br />“You say that to me… and if you’re not careful you might end up stuck with me.” It was a warning. <br /><br />“You’re making this difficult.” Her eyes never moved from his face. “I think that’s what I’m trying to tell you. I want to be stuck with you.”</b><br /><br />This is my first book by this author but it likely won’t be my last. I loved the characters,her writing was solid, the steam level was good.I think the author really succeeded in touching on a lot of serious topics but still keeping the story a sweet, sexy read. Most of the romances I read, I enjoy but quickly forget. Christopher is probably a hero I'll be thinking about for a while. <b>FOUR "FEEL GOOD" STARS for Beast!</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3951122388606122798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6553958131561906612">This is the story of Christopher large scarred Marine. He was born with a bilateral cleft lip, palate and had facial deformities. His family was poor and did not have the money to have it fixed properly. The surgeon that repaired it, left him horribly scarred and, because he is so large, he is terrifying to look at. The heroine, Ashleigh, is overweight short and has just been dumped by her boyfriend (who married someone else while dating her). She has believes she needs to lose weight but does n</span>
  <span id="freeText6553958131561906612" style="display:none">This is the story of Christopher large scarred Marine. He was born with a bilateral cleft lip, palate and had facial deformities. His family was poor and did not have the money to have it fixed properly. The surgeon that repaired it, left him horribly scarred and, because he is so large, he is terrifying to look at. The heroine, Ashleigh, is overweight short and has just been dumped by her boyfriend (who married someone else while dating her). She has believes she needs to lose weight but does not want to workout in front of others. She begins to workout in the sub-basement gym of her company's building, where she meets Christoper. This is a very sweet story and the romance is written beautifully. I particularly appreciated the medical facts. Not many people know the pain that kids with cleft lips and palates go through. I would definitely loan this book. TTFN-Sandy</span>

  <span id="freeText10855533145931771139" style="display:none">02/17/2013 -- Brief Rating explanation<br /><b><br />Overall Rating = 3 Stars<br />Book Cover / Book Blurb = 3 / 2 = 2.5 Stars<br />Writer’s Voice = 3 Stars<br />Character Development = 4 Stars<br />Story Appreciation = 3.5 Stars<br />Worth the Chili = 2 Stars [$4.99 Amazon – not available B&amp;N]<br /></b><br /><br />This is an inter-racial story taken loosely from the Disney "Beauty &amp; the Beast" model. When you read the blurb you think this H gets wounded causing the extensive facial damage. This is not the case. The heroine is a larger, light skinned African American girl with real self-image issues. In the end these two come together in a decently written story. This book was recommended by a few people on a string I follow. Glad I got this opportunity and will be on the lookout for other books by this author.<br /><br />For a different twist in a time worn tale, check this one out.<br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

  <span id="freeText3259043344589677979" style="display:none">This was fantastic. Loved it! You never know what a person goes through in their own skin. I could feel how each person felt whether is was weight or a facial disfigurement. This author touched on so many things in the book. Bulimia, Racism, dementia, etc. Beauty should be seen from the inside, but in this day and age it isn't. The two most unlikely people fell in love. Now, how many times have you seen a couple in real life and couldn't figure how they got together. You never know who you will fall in love with. Excellent read! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3385076715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3385076715" />
    <a title="Jite" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65154349-jite"><img alt="Jite" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512649140p2/65154349.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3385076715?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jite" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jite" href="/user/show/65154349-jite">Jite</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3385076715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16789523027981374676">I really liked this beauty and the beast trope book with a twist. It features Ashleigh, a black plus-sized, beautiful, professionally successful heroine with a myriad of insecurities and Christopher, a white marine who is considered ugly and “beastly” due to reasons out of his control who meet each other at a point where they’re both exactly what the other needs.<br/><br/>I like that this romance explores a relatable relationship of getting to know someone becoming friends before starting a relationship. </span>
  <span id="freeText16789523027981374676" style="display:none">I really liked this beauty and the beast trope book with a twist. It features Ashleigh, a black plus-sized, beautiful, professionally successful heroine with a myriad of insecurities and Christopher, a white marine who is considered ugly and “beastly” due to reasons out of his control who meet each other at a point where they’re both exactly what the other needs.<br /><br />I like that this romance explores a relatable relationship of getting to know someone becoming friends before starting a relationship. I like that Christopher is somewhat of an innocent and shy and not necessarily overtly alpha despite his hulking looks. I like that Ashleigh sort of has the power in the relationship and even when Christopher is helping and supporting her in achieving her goals, it never feels like he’s “saving” her in any way.<br /><br />This book deals with a lot of deep issues around physical appearance. If you’ve ever struggled with low self esteem or an eating disorder, you need to be mindful that this contains a considerable amount of that kind of content if you’re going to be triggered. There are some mental health issues at play here that I don’t think were really dealt with as deeply as the issues were treated but I thought this was great. I didn’t need the extra special ending with the Beast but I didn’t mind it, I just don’t think it added to the book’s central theme of inner beauty.<br /><br />I also like the way race was dealt with in this interracial romance. It wasn’t a non-issue, but it also wasn’t a central issue to be beaten upon endlessly as if the only reason the hero and the heroine were together or had any relationship conflict was because of their race. It was an issue that both characters acknowledged and cared about and wanted to protect each other from, it was a concern how the outer world would react, but it wasn’t an issue for them as couple of human beings in love. I really liked this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16789523027981374676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_32854489'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32854489-broken"><img alt="Broken" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1478034340l/32854489._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GgcW7r+JaJJMvnWuHCcsxxq1Q2cjvemRseRXHMJWFX1xZ9mTiqA1cyU9NbUGHgnw+93l74YHzoAExp4BS7UFqA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MeJNwgfyN/uU6akKegrS4fkATEVzxAEzgdZp5FnIsrFagoK/MttqGv1q6RFgM/fWGGjqzdZ+JiI09KD50CuiZA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer16449003312044191285">Who is Pepper Pace?<br/><br/>Pepper Pace is the pen name used by the author. Born and raised in Cincinnati, she has always enjoyed creativity. At a very young age, Pepper had a gift for art and would spend most of her spare time drawing images that she later began adding stories behind. Soon writing became more important than the illustrations and though she still loved art, it took a back seat to her real </span>
  <span id="freeText16449003312044191285" style="display:none">Who is Pepper Pace?<br /><br />Pepper Pace is the pen name used by the author. Born and raised in Cincinnati, she has always enjoyed creativity. At a very young age, Pepper had a gift for art and would spend most of her spare time drawing images that she later began adding stories behind. Soon writing became more important than the illustrations and though she still loved art, it took a back seat to her real love.<br /><br />Pepper wrote her first novel when she was 12 years old and had written 2 more by the age of 18. Too shy to share her work with anyone, Pepper stock piled her many stories into notebooks until she came upon Literotica.com and was compelled to share her craft.<br /><br />Pepper became instantly popular and won several awards each year in which she submitted a story to the site. After receiving popular feedback, she grew in confidence and created a popular blog entitled Writing Feedback where she encourages her readers to interact with her on topics concerning, music, writing, art and pop culture, and can be contacted at her blog:<br />pepperpacefeedback.blogspot.com/<br /><br />Pepper lives in Cincinnati where many of her characters also reside.<br /><br />Other Websites:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pepperpacefeedback.blogspot.com/">http://pepperpacefeedback.blogspot.com/</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pepperpace.tumblr.com/">http://pepperpace.tumblr.com/</a></span>
